	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">1988 Summer Olympics</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

<p>The <b>1988 Summer Olympics</b> (<a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a> <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>&#58;&#160;<span lang="ko-Hang" title="Korean language text">서울 하계 올림픽</span>&#59; <a href="/wiki/Revised_Romanization_of_Korean" title="Revised Romanization of Korean">RR</a>&#58;&#160;<i><i lang="ko-Latn" title="Korean-language romanization">Seoul Hagye Ollimpik</i></i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Korean" title="Help:IPA/Korean">[sʌ.ul ɦaɡje olːimpʰik]</a></span>), officially known as the <b>Games of the XXIV Olympiad</b>, was an international <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> celebrated from 17 September to 2 October 1988 in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>.
</p><p>In the Seoul Games, 159 nations were represented by a total of 8,391 athletes: 6,197 men and 2,194 women. 237 events were held and 27,221 volunteers helped to prepare the Olympics. 11,331 media (4,978 <a href="/wiki/Print_media" class="mw-redirect" title="Print media">written press</a> and 6,353 <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_media" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadcast media">broadcasters</a>) showed the Games all over the world.<sup id="cite_ref-SEOUL_1988_Games_of_the_XXIV_Olympiad_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEOUL_1988_Games_of_the_XXIV_Olympiad-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>These were the last Olympic Games for the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_at_the_Olympics" title="Soviet Union at the Olympics">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Germany_at_the_Olympics" title="East Germany at the Olympics">East Germany</a>, as both ceased to exist before the next Olympic Games. The Soviets utterly dominated the medal table, winning 55 gold and 132 total medals. No country came close to this result after 1988.
</p><p>The games were boycotted by <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and its ally, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Republic_of_Ethiopia" title="People&#39;s Democratic Republic of Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania" title="People&#39;s Socialist Republic of Albania">Albania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> did not respond to the invitations sent by the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">IOC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FindlingPelle1996_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FindlingPelle1996-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> did not participate due to athletic and financial considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-Janofsky_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janofsky-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The participation of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Democratic Republic of Madagascar">Madagascar</a> had been expected, and their team was expected at the opening ceremony of 160 nations. However, the country withdrew because of financial reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, the much larger boycotts seen in the previous three Summer Olympics (<a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">1976</a>, <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980</a> and <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">1984</a>) were avoided, resulting in the largest number of participating nations during the Cold War era.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_city_selection">Host city selection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Host city selection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Seoul was chosen to host the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics">Summer Games</a> through a vote held on 30 September 1981, finishing ahead of the Japanese city of <a href="/wiki/Nagoya" title="Nagoya">Nagoya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SEOUL_1988_Games_of_the_XXIV_Olympiad_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEOUL_1988_Games_of_the_XXIV_Olympiad-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Below was the vote count that occurred at the 84th <a href="/wiki/IOC_Session" class="mw-redirect" title="IOC Session">IOC Session</a> and 11th <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Congress" title="Olympic Congress">Olympic Congress</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baden-Baden" title="Baden-Baden">Baden-Baden</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<td style="text-align:center;">27
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>After the Olympics were awarded, Seoul also received the opportunity to stage the 10th <a href="/wiki/1986_Asian_Games" title="1986 Asian Games">Asian Games</a> in 1986, using them to test its preparation for the Olympics.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Highlights">Highlights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Highlights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seoul_Olympic_torch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Seoul_Olympic_torch.jpg/220px-Seoul_Olympic_torch.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Seoul_Olympic_torch.jpg/330px-Seoul_Olympic_torch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Seoul_Olympic_torch.jpg/440px-Seoul_Olympic_torch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2800" data-file-height="1870" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seoul_Olympic_torch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South Koreans stand next to the 1988 Summer Olympic cauldron</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fireworks_at_the_closing_ceremonies_of_the_1988_Summer_Games.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Fireworks_at_the_closing_ceremonies_of_the_1988_Summer_Games.JPEG/220px-Fireworks_at_the_closing_ceremonies_of_the_1988_Summer_Games.JPEG" decoding="async" width="220" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Fireworks_at_the_closing_ceremonies_of_the_1988_Summer_Games.JPEG/330px-Fireworks_at_the_closing_ceremonies_of_the_1988_Summer_Games.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Fireworks_at_the_closing_ceremonies_of_the_1988_Summer_Games.JPEG/440px-Fireworks_at_the_closing_ceremonies_of_the_1988_Summer_Games.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="2830" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fireworks_at_the_closing_ceremonies_of_the_1988_Summer_Games.JPEG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fireworks at the closing ceremony of the 1988 Summer Olympics</div></div></div>
<ul><li>In its final Olympics, the Soviet Union utterly dominated the medal table winning 55 gold and 132 total medals. No country came close to this result after 1988.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Artemov" title="Vladimir Artemov">Vladimir Artemov</a> won four gold medals in gymnastics.<sup id="cite_ref-Honored_Inductees_-_Vladimir_Artemov_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Honored_Inductees_-_Vladimir_Artemov-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daniela_Siliva%C5%9F" class="mw-redirect" title="Daniela Silivaş">Daniela Silivaş</a> of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">Romania</a> won three and equalled compatriot <a href="/wiki/Nadia_Com%C4%83neci" title="Nadia Comăneci">Nadia Comăneci</a>'s record of seven <a href="/wiki/Perfect_10_(gymnastics)" title="Perfect 10 (gymnastics)">Perfect 10s</a> in one Olympic Games.<sup id="cite_ref-Honored_Inductees_-_Daniela_Silivas_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Honored_Inductees_-_Daniela_Silivas-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>After having demolished the world record in the 100&#160;m dash at the Olympic Trials in Indianapolis, U.S. sprinter <a href="/wiki/Florence_Griffith_Joyner" title="Florence Griffith Joyner">Florence Griffith Joyner</a> set an Olympic record (10.62) in the 100-metre dash and a still-standing world record (21.34) in the 200-metre dash to capture gold medals in both events. To these medals, she added a gold in the 4×100 relay and a silver in the 4×400.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Sport_-_Florence_Griffith-Joyner_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Sport_-_Florence_Griffith-Joyner-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Canadian <a href="/wiki/Ben_Johnson_(Canadian_sprinter)" title="Ben Johnson (Canadian sprinter)">Ben Johnson</a> won <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1988_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_100_metres" title="Athletics at the 1988 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s 100 metres">the 100&#160;m final</a> with a new world record, but was disqualified after he tested positive for <a href="/wiki/Stanozolol" title="Stanozolol">stanozolol</a>. Johnson has since claimed that his positive test was the result of sabotage.<sup id="cite_ref-Odd_tale_of_mystery_man_in_waiting-room_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Odd_tale_of_mystery_man_in_waiting-room-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ben_Johnson_acusa_a_EEUU_de_proteger_a_sus_atletas_dopados_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ben_Johnson_acusa_a_EEUU_de_proteger_a_sus_atletas_dopados-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics_at_the_1988_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_artistic_team_all-around" title="Gymnastics at the 1988 Summer Olympics – Women&#39;s artistic team all-around">Women's Artistic Gymnastics Team All-Around Competition</a>, the U.S. women's team was penalized with a deduction of five tenths of a point from their team score by the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Gymnastics" class="mw-redirect" title="International Federation of Gymnastics">Fédération Internationale de Gymnastique (FIG)</a> after the compulsory round due to their Olympic team alternate Rhonda Faehn appearing on the podium for the uneven bars during the duration of <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Garrison-Funderburk" class="mw-redirect" title="Kelly Garrison-Funderburk">Kelly Garrison-Steve's</a> compulsory <a href="/wiki/Uneven_bars_(gymnastics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Uneven bars (gymnastics)">uneven bars</a> routine, despite not competing, having been caught by the East German judge, Ellen Berger. The U.S. finished fourth after the completion of the optional rounds with a combined score of 390.575, three tenths of a point behind <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>. This still remains controversial in the sport of gymnastics, as the U.S. performed better than the East German team and they would have taken the bronze medal in the team competition had they not been penalized or had an inquiry accepted to receive the points back.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Phoebe_Mills" title="Phoebe Mills">Phoebe Mills</a> won an individual bronze medal on the balance beam, shared with Romania's <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Potorac" title="Gabriela Potorac">Gabriela Potorac</a>, making history as the first medal (team or individual) ever won by a U.S. woman in artistic gymnastics at a fully attended games.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">USSR (Soviet Union)</a> won their final team gold medals in artistic gymnastics on both the men's and women's sides with scores of 593.350 and 395.475 respectively. The men's team was led by <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Artemov" title="Vladimir Artemov">Vladimir Artemov</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Elena_Shushunova" class="mw-redirect" title="Elena Shushunova">Elena Shushunova</a> lead the women's team.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Lemieux" title="Lawrence Lemieux">Lawrence Lemieux</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">Canadian</a> sailor in the <a href="/wiki/Finn_(dinghy)" title="Finn (dinghy)">Finn class</a>, was in second place and poised to win a silver medal when he abandoned the race to save an injured competitor. He arrived in 21st place, but was recognized by the IOC with the <a href="/wiki/Pierre_de_Coubertin_medal" title="Pierre de Coubertin medal">Pierre de Coubertin medal</a> honoring his bravery and sacrifice.</li>
<li>U.S. diver <a href="/wiki/Greg_Louganis" title="Greg Louganis">Greg Louganis</a> won back-to-back titles on both diving events despite hitting his head on the springboard in the third round and suffering a concussion.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christa_Luding-Rothenburger" title="Christa Luding-Rothenburger">Christa Luding-Rothenburger</a> of <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> became the first (and only) athlete to win Olympic medals at the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympics</a> and Summer Olympics in the same year. She added a cycling silver to the <a href="/wiki/Speed_skating" title="Speed skating">speed skating</a> gold she won earlier in the <a href="/wiki/1988_Winter_Olympics" title="1988 Winter Olympics">Winter Olympics of that year</a> in <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Christa_Luding-Rothenburger_Encyclopædia_Britannica_article_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christa_Luding-Rothenburger_Encyclopædia_Britannica_article-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anthony_Nesty" title="Anthony Nesty">Anthony Nesty</a> of <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> won his country's first Olympic medal by winning the 100&#160;m <a href="/wiki/Butterfly_stroke" title="Butterfly stroke">butterfly</a>, scoring an upset victory over <a href="/wiki/Matt_Biondi" title="Matt Biondi">Matt Biondi</a> by .01 of a second (thwarting Biondi's attempt<sup id="cite_ref-Odds_against_Phelps_eclipsing_Spitz_-_Biondi_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Odds_against_Phelps_eclipsing_Spitz_-_Biondi-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> of breaking <a href="/wiki/Mark_Spitz" title="Mark Spitz">Mark Spitz</a>' record seven golds in one Olympic event); he was the first <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">black person</a> to win an individual swimming gold.<sup id="cite_ref-El_deporte_en_el_Sur_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El_deporte_en_el_Sur-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Swimmer <a href="/wiki/Kristin_Otto" title="Kristin Otto">Kristin Otto</a> of East Germany won six gold medals. Other multi-medalists in the pool were <a href="/wiki/Matt_Biondi" title="Matt Biondi">Matt Biondi</a> (five)<sup id="cite_ref-United_States_Olympic_Committee_-_Biondi,_Matt_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_States_Olympic_Committee_-_Biondi,_Matt-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Janet_Evans" title="Janet Evans">Janet Evans</a> (three).<sup id="cite_ref-United_States_Olympic_Committee_-_Evans,_Janet_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_States_Olympic_Committee_-_Evans,_Janet-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Swedish</a> <a href="/wiki/Fencing" title="Fencing">fencer</a> <a href="/wiki/Kerstin_Palm" title="Kerstin Palm">Kerstin Palm</a> became the first woman to take part in seven Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-SEOUL_1988_Games_of_the_XXIV_Olympiad_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEOUL_1988_Games_of_the_XXIV_Olympiad-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Swimmer <a href="/wiki/Melvin_Stewart" title="Melvin Stewart">Mel Stewart</a> of the U.S. was the most anticipated to win the men's 200&#160;m butterfly final<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> but surprisingly, came in 5th.<sup id="cite_ref-Nuoto_-_risultati_200m._farfalla_uomini_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nuoto_-_risultati_200m._farfalla_uomini-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Todd_(equestrian)" title="Mark Todd (equestrian)">Mark Todd</a> of New Zealand won his second consecutive individual gold medal in the three-day event in equestrian on <a href="/wiki/Charisma_(horse)" title="Charisma (horse)">Charisma</a>, only the second time in eventing history that a gold medal has been won consecutively.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Awards_:_1980-1989_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Awards_:_1980-1989-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Baseball<sup id="cite_ref-Demonstration_Sports_at_the_Olympic_Games_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demonstration_Sports_at_the_Olympic_Games-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">Taekwondo</a><sup id="cite_ref-About_WTF_-_History_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_WTF_-_History-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> were demonstration sports. The opening ceremony featured a mass demonstration of taekwondo with hundreds of adults and children performing moves in unison.</li>
<li>This was the last time the U.S. was represented by a basketball team that did not feature <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> players (featuring college players);<sup id="cite_ref-The_Original_Dream_Team_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Original_Dream_Team-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> the team won the bronze medal after being defeated by the Soviet Union (that was represented by veteran professionals) which went on to win the gold medal.<sup id="cite_ref-THE_SEOUL_OLYMPICS:_Men&#39;s_Basketball;_After_16-Year_Wait,_Soviets_Stun_U.S._Again,_82-76_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE_SEOUL_OLYMPICS:_Men&#39;s_Basketball;_After_16-Year_Wait,_Soviets_Stun_U.S._Again,_82-76-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>For the first time in history, all the <a href="/wiki/Dressage" title="Dressage">dressage</a> events were won by women.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_at_the_1988_Summer_Olympics_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada_at_the_1988_Summer_Olympics-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Women's <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a> was held for the first time, as a demonstration sport.<sup id="cite_ref-Obukan_Judo_History_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Obukan_Judo_History-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Bowling was held as a demonstration sport, with Kwon Jong Yul of South Korea and Arianne Cerdeña from the Philippines winning the men's and women's gold medals, respectively.</li>
<li>Table tennis was introduced at the Olympics, with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and South Korea both winning two titles.<sup id="cite_ref-Olympic_Table_Tennis_Champions_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olympic_Table_Tennis_Champions-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Tennis returned to the Olympics after a 64-year absence,<sup id="cite_ref-THE_SEOUL_OLYMPICS:_Tennis;_Tennis_Returns_to_Good_Reviews_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE_SEOUL_OLYMPICS:_Tennis;_Tennis_Returns_to_Good_Reviews-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Steffi_Graf" title="Steffi Graf">Steffi Graf</a> added to her four <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> victories in the year by also winning the Olympic title,<sup id="cite_ref-Steffi_graf,_la_mejor_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steffi_graf,_la_mejor-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> beating <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Sabatini" title="Gabriela Sabatini">Sabatini</a> in the final.<sup id="cite_ref-Gabriela_Sabatini_-_Fotos,_Vídeos,_Biografía,_Wallpapers_y_Ficha_Técnica_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gabriela_Sabatini_-_Fotos,_Vídeos,_Biografía,_Wallpapers_y_Ficha_Técnica-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Two <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_People%27s_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian People&#39;s Republic">Bulgarian</a> <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifters</a> were stripped of their gold medals after failing doping tests, and the team withdrew after this event.<sup id="cite_ref-THE_SEOUL_OLYMPICS:_Weight_Lifting;_Team_Lifted_After_2d_Drug_Test_Is_Failed_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE_SEOUL_OLYMPICS:_Weight_Lifting;_Team_Lifted_After_2d_Drug_Test_Is_Failed-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In boxing, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Jones_Jr." title="Roy Jones Jr.">Roy Jones Jr.</a> of the U.S. dominated his opponents, never losing a single round en route to the final. In the final, he controversially lost a 3–2 decision to South Korean fighter <a href="/wiki/Park_Si-Hun" class="mw-redirect" title="Park Si-Hun">Park Si-Hun</a> despite pummeling Park for three rounds and landing 86 punches to Park's 32.<sup id="cite_ref-query.nytimes.com_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-query.nytimes.com-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-times_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Seoul_Games_scarred_by_riots_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seoul_Games_scarred_by_riots-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Another boxing controversy involved a match between South Korea's Jong-il Byun and Bulgaria's Alexander Hristov.  A random spectator ran around "winding up" the crowd before the match and New Zealander referee Keith Walker repeated warned Jong-Il regarding headbutting.  When the decision went against Jong-il, a sub-set of spectators stormed the ring and attacked Walker, with South Korean Olympic officials and security guards also kicking him before his fellow referees pulled him away.<sup id="cite_ref-Seoul_Games_scarred_by_riots_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seoul_Games_scarred_by_riots-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In yet another boxing controversy, <a href="/wiki/Riddick_Bowe" title="Riddick Bowe">Riddick Bowe</a> of the US lost a controversial match in the finals to future world heavyweight champion <a href="/wiki/Lennox_Lewis" title="Lennox Lewis">Lennox Lewis</a>. Bowe had a dominant first round, landing 33 of 94 punches thrown (34%) while Lewis landed 14 of 67 (21%). In the first round the referee from <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> gave Bowe two cautions for headbutts and deducted a point for a third headbutt, although replay clearly showed there was no headbutt. Commentator <a href="/wiki/Ferdie_Pacheco" title="Ferdie Pacheco">Ferdie Pacheco</a> disagreed with the deduction, saying they did not hit heads. In the second round, Lewis landed several hard punches. The referee gave Bowe two <a href="/wiki/Standing_eight_count" title="Standing eight count">standing eight counts</a> and waved the fight off after the second one, even though Bowe seemed able to continue. Pacheco disagreed with the stoppage, calling it "very strange."<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Soviet <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifter</a> <a href="/wiki/Yury_Zakharevich" title="Yury Zakharevich">Yury Zakharevich</a> won the men's heavyweight (up to 110&#160;kg class) with a 210&#160;kg snatch and 245&#160;kg clean and jerk for a 455&#160;kg total. Zakhareivich had dislocated his elbow in 1983 attempting a world record and had it rebuilt with synthetic tendons.</li>
<li>Indonesia gained its first medal in Olympic history when the women's team won a silver medal in archery.</li></ul>
<p>Live doves were released during the opening ceremony as a symbol of world peace, but a number of the doves were burned alive or suffered major trauma by the lighting of the Olympic cauldron. As a result of protests following the incident, the last time live doves were released at the opening ceremony was in 1992 in Barcelona, hours before the flame was lit. Balloon doves were released in 1994 at the Lillehammer Winter Games and paper doves were used at the Atlanta Ceremony in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>These were also the last Summer Olympic Games to hold the Opening Ceremony during the daytime. The opening ceremony featured a skydiving team descending over the stadium and forming the five-colored Olympic Rings,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> as well as a mass demonstration of <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">taekwondo</a>. The skydiving team trained at <a href="/wiki/Yolo_County_Airport" title="Yolo County Airport">SkyDance SkyDiving</a> and had hoped the opening ceremony appearance would set the stage for skydiving becoming a medal event by 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-skydance_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skydance-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Significance_of_1988_Olympics_in_South_Korea">Significance of 1988 Olympics in South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Significance of 1988 Olympics in South Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seoul.Olympic.Stadium.01_copy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Seoul.Olympic.Stadium.01_copy.jpg/220px-Seoul.Olympic.Stadium.01_copy.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Seoul.Olympic.Stadium.01_copy.jpg/330px-Seoul.Olympic.Stadium.01_copy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Seoul.Olympic.Stadium.01_copy.jpg/440px-Seoul.Olympic.Stadium.01_copy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="1512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seoul.Olympic.Stadium.01_copy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Olympic_Stadium" title="Seoul Olympic Stadium">Seoul Olympic Stadium</a> seen from <a href="/wiki/Han_River_(Korea)" title="Han River (Korea)">Han River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Hosting the 1988 Olympics presented an opportunity to bring international attention to South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The idea for South Korea to place a bid for the 1988 Games emerged during the last days of the <a href="/wiki/Park_Chung-hee" title="Park Chung-hee">Park Chung-hee</a> administration in the late 1970s.  After President Park's assassination in 1979, <a href="/wiki/Chun_Doo-hwan" title="Chun Doo-hwan">Chun Doo-hwan</a>, his successor, submitted Korea's bid to the IOC in September 1981, in hopes that the increased international exposure brought by the Olympics would legitimize his authoritarian regime amidst increasing political pressure for democratization, provide protection from increasing threats from <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, and showcase the <a href="/wiki/Miracle_on_the_Han_River" title="Miracle on the Han River">Korean economic miracle</a> to the world community.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> South Korea was awarded the bid on 30 September 1981, becoming the 20th host nation (16th in the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympics</a>), as well as the second Asian nation (following Japan in the <a href="/wiki/1964_Summer_Olympics" title="1964 Summer Olympics">1964 Summer Olympics</a>) and the first mainland Asian nation.
</p><p>Copying the model of 1964 Tokyo Olympics as a rite of passage for the Japanese economy and re-integration of Japan in the family of nations in the post-war era, the South Korean government hoped to use the Olympics as a "coming-out party".  The Olympics gave a powerful impetus to the development of South Korea's relations with Eastern Europe, the Soviet Union and with China.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In utilizing media events theory, Larson and Park investigated the 1988 Seoul Olympics as a form of political communication. They revealed the significance of South Korea's military government throughout the period of the Olympic bid and preparation, followed by the many advantages of the Seoul Olympics: rapid economic modernization, social mobilization and the legitimization of the military dictatorship.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Expansion_of_.22vagrant.22_camps_prior_to_Olympics"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_of_&quot;vagrant&quot;_camps_prior_to_Olympics">Expansion of "vagrant" camps prior to Olympics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Expansion of &quot;vagrant&quot; camps prior to Olympics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22">"1988 Summer Olympics"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Existing camps for "vagrants" (homeless persons) were ramped up prior to the 1988 Olympics. An Associated Press article states that homeless and alcoholic persons, "but mostly children and the disabled" were arrested and sent to these camps to prepare for the Olympics. In addition, a prosecutor had his investigation into the Brothers Home camp limited at a number of levels of government "in part out of fear of an embarrassing international incident on the eve of the Olympics."<sup id="cite_ref-Associated_Press_2016-04-20_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Associated_Press_2016-04-20-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1975, the previous president of South Korea had begun a policy of rounding up vagrants.  According to government documents obtained by the Associated Press, from 1981 to 1986 the number of persons held increased from 8,600 to more than 16,000. Police officers often received promotions based on the number of vagrants they had arrested, and owners of facilities received a subsidy based on the number of persons held. There were multiple reports of inmates being raped or beaten, and sometimes beaten to death.<sup id="cite_ref-Associated_Press_2016-04-20_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Associated_Press_2016-04-20-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>4,000 of these "vagrants" were held at the Brothers Home facility. Many of the guards were former inmates who had been "promoted" because of loyalty to the camp's owner. Various money-making operations were conducted such as manufacturing ball-point pens and fishing hooks, as well as clothing for Daewoo. Only a few inmates were paid belatedly for this work.<sup id="cite_ref-Associated_Press_2016-04-20_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Associated_Press_2016-04-20-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By accident while on a hunting trip, prosecutor Kim Yong Won heard about and visited a work detail of prisoners in ragged clothes being overseen by guards with wooden bats and dogs. In his words, he knew immediately that "a very serious crime" was occurring. And in January 1987, he led a raid on the facility and found beaten and malnourished inmates. However, he received political pressure at various levels to reduce the charges against the owner, managers, and guards. In the end, the owner only served two-and-a-half years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-Associated_Press_2016-04-20_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Associated_Press_2016-04-20-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Brothers Home was a religious facility based on the Christian faith. There were in fact inspections by both city officials and church officials. However, these were scheduled inspections in which healthier inmates were presented in carefully planned and orchestrated circumstances. There were no unannounced inspections.<sup id="cite_ref-Associated_Press_2016-04-20_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Associated_Press_2016-04-20-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1990s, construction workers found about 100 human bones on a mountainside outside the location of the former Brothers Home.<sup id="cite_ref-Associated_Press_2016-04-20_46-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Associated_Press_2016-04-20-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1988_Summer_Olympics_boycott">1988 Summer Olympics boycott</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1988 Summer Olympics boycott">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22">"1988 Summer Olympics"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%221988+Summer+Olympics%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2010</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1988_Summer_Olympics_(Seoul)_boycotting_countries_(blue).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/1988_Summer_Olympics_%28Seoul%29_boycotting_countries_%28blue%29.png/370px-1988_Summer_Olympics_%28Seoul%29_boycotting_countries_%28blue%29.png" decoding="async" width="370" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/1988_Summer_Olympics_%28Seoul%29_boycotting_countries_%28blue%29.png/555px-1988_Summer_Olympics_%28Seoul%29_boycotting_countries_%28blue%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/1988_Summer_Olympics_%28Seoul%29_boycotting_countries_%28blue%29.png/740px-1988_Summer_Olympics_%28Seoul%29_boycotting_countries_%28blue%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1988_Summer_Olympics_(Seoul)_boycotting_countries_(blue).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries boycotting or absent from the 1988 Games are shaded blue</div></div></div>
<p>In preparation for the 1988 Olympics, the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a>  worked to prevent another Olympic boycott by the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> as had happened at the <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">1984 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>. This was made more difficult by the lack of diplomatic relations between South Korea and communist countries. This prompted action by the IOC president <a href="/wiki/Juan_Antonio_Samaranch" title="Juan Antonio Samaranch">Juan Antonio Samaranch</a>, who was committed to the participation of these countries. Thus, at the Assembly of National Olympic Committees in Mexico City in November 1984, the "Mexico Declaration" <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://library.la84.org/OlympicInformationCenter/OlympicReview/1984/ore206/ORE206e.pdf">[1]</a> was adopted; by it, the participants agreed to include the host of the Olympic Games in 1988.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The agreement of the Soviet Union was reached in 1987. After the Los Angeles games, <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> had already decided to participate again in Seoul. The IOC also decided that it would send invitations to the 1988 Games itself and did not leave this task to the organizing committee as had been done before. Despite these developments, behind the scenes, the IOC did consider relocating the Games and explored the suitability of <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> as an alternative.
</p><p>Another point of conflict was the involvement of <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> in hosting the Games, something that had been encouraged by Cuban president <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>, who called for North Korea to be considered joint host of the Games. As a result, on 8 and 9 January 1986 in <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, the IOC President chaired a meeting of the North and South Korean Olympic Committees. North Korea demanded that eleven of the 23 Olympic sports be carried out on its territory, and also demanded special opening and closing ceremonies. It wanted a joint organizing committee and a united team. The negotiations were continued into another meeting, but were not successful. The IOC did not meet the demands of North Korea and only about half of the desired sporting events were offered to the North. So the focus thereafter was solely on Seoul and South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The games were boycotted by <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and its ally, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Republic_of_Ethiopia" title="People&#39;s Democratic Republic of Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania" title="People&#39;s Socialist Republic of Albania">Albania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> did not respond to the invitations sent by the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">IOC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FindlingPelle1996_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FindlingPelle1996-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> did not participate due to athletic and financial considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-Janofsky_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janofsky-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The participation of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Democratic Republic of Madagascar">Madagascar</a> had been expected, and their team was expected at the opening ceremony of 160 nations. However, the country withdrew for financial reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_theme_song">Official theme song</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Official theme song">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seoul_1988_Torch.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Seoul_1988_Torch.JPG/220px-Seoul_1988_Torch.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Seoul_1988_Torch.JPG/330px-Seoul_1988_Torch.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Seoul_1988_Torch.JPG/440px-Seoul_1988_Torch.JPG 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seoul_1988_Torch.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The official <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Torch" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Torch">Olympic Torch</a> used during the 1988 Summer Olympics in Seoul.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hand_in_Hand_(Olympic_theme_song)" title="Hand in Hand (Olympic theme song)">Hand in Hand (Olympic theme song)</a></div>
<p>In 1988, the Seoul Olympic Organizing Committee (SLOOC) decided to produce and distribute an official song of the Seoul Games to publicize the Games to all the IOC member nations, encouraging their participation in the festival and
consolidating the harmony and friendship of the entire world citizens through the song. The song "<a href="/wiki/Hand_in_Hand_(Olympics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hand in Hand (Olympics)">Hand in Hand</a>" was written by Italian composer <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Moroder" title="Giorgio Moroder">Giorgio Moroder</a> and American songwriter <a href="/wiki/Tom_Whitlock" title="Tom Whitlock">Tom Whitlock</a>, and performed by singing group Koreana.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Venues_of_the_1988_Summer_Olympics" title="Venues of the 1988 Summer Olympics">Venues of the 1988 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Khitai6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Khitai6.jpg/220px-Khitai6.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Khitai6.jpg/330px-Khitai6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Khitai6.jpg/440px-Khitai6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Khitai6.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Park,_Seoul" title="Olympic Park, Seoul">World Peace Gate</a> in Seoul.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seoul_Olympic_Swimming_Pool.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Seoul_Olympic_Swimming_Pool.jpg/220px-Seoul_Olympic_Swimming_Pool.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Seoul_Olympic_Swimming_Pool.jpg/330px-Seoul_Olympic_Swimming_Pool.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Seoul_Olympic_Swimming_Pool.jpg/440px-Seoul_Olympic_Swimming_Pool.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seoul_Olympic_Swimming_Pool.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jamsil_Indoor_Swimming_Pool" title="Jamsil Indoor Swimming Pool">Jamsil Indoor Swimming Pool</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Autumn_Seoul_Olympic_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Autumn_Seoul_Olympic_Park.jpg/220px-Autumn_Seoul_Olympic_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Autumn_Seoul_Olympic_Park.jpg/330px-Autumn_Seoul_Olympic_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Autumn_Seoul_Olympic_Park.jpg/440px-Autumn_Seoul_Olympic_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Autumn_Seoul_Olympic_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Park,_Seoul" title="Olympic Park, Seoul">Seoul Olympic Park</a> in autumn.</div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Seoul_Sports_Complex" title="Seoul Sports Complex">Seoul Sports Complex</a> venues
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Seoul)" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Stadium (Seoul)">Seoul Olympic Stadium</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_E"><a href="#endnote_E">[E]</a></sup> – opening/closing ceremonies, athletics, equestrian (jumping individual final), football (final)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jamsil_Indoor_Swimming_Pool" title="Jamsil Indoor Swimming Pool">Jamsil Indoor Swimming Pool</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_E"><a href="#endnote_E">[E]</a></sup> – diving, modern pentathlon (swimming), synchronized swimming, swimming, water polo</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jamsil_Gymnasium" class="mw-redirect" title="Jamsil Gymnasium">Jamsil Gymnasium</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_E"><a href="#endnote_E">[E]</a></sup> – basketball, volleyball (final)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jamsil_Students%27_Gymnasium" title="Jamsil Students&#39; Gymnasium">Jamsil Students' Gymnasium</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_E"><a href="#endnote_E">[E]</a></sup> – boxing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jamsil_Baseball_Stadium" title="Jamsil Baseball Stadium">Jamsil Baseball Stadium</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_E"><a href="#endnote_E">[E]</a></sup> – baseball (demonstration)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Park,_Seoul" title="Olympic Park, Seoul">Olympic Park</a> venues
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Velodrome_(Seoul)" title="Olympic Velodrome (Seoul)">Olympic Velodrome</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_N"><a href="#endnote_N">[N]</a></sup> – cycling (track)</li>

<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_E"><sup>E</sup></span>  Existing facilities modified or refurbished in preparation for the Olympic Games.<br />
<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_N"><sup>N</sup></span>  New facilities constructed in preparation for the Olympic Games.

</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost">Cost</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cost">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to <i>The Oxford Olympics Study</i> data is not available to establish the cost of the Seoul 1988 Summer Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Average cost for Summer Games since 1960, for which data are available, is US$5.2 billion.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 1988 Summer Olympics featured 23 different sports encompassing 31 disciplines, and medals were awarded in 237 events. In the list below, the number of events in each discipline is noted in parentheses.
</p>
<div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_National_Olympic_Committees">Participating National Olympic Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Participating National Olympic Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1988_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/1988_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png/220px-1988_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/1988_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png/330px-1988_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/1988_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png/440px-1988_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1988_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Participants (blue nations had their first entrance).</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1988_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1988_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif/220px-1988_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1988_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif/330px-1988_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1988_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif/440px-1988_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1988_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Number of athletes sent by each nation.</div></div></div>
<p>Athletes from 159 nations competed at the Seoul Games.  <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Republic_of_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Democratic Republic of Yemen">South Yemen</a> made their first Olympic appearance at these Games. <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> made their first Summer Olympic appearance at these games having participated in the <a href="/wiki/1988_Winter_Olympics" title="1988 Winter Olympics">1988 Winter Olympics</a> in Calgary.
</p><p>In the following list, the number in parentheses indicates the number of athletes from each nation that competed in Seoul:<sup id="cite_ref-Olympic_Games_Participating_Countries_-_1988_Seoul_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olympic_Games_Participating_Countries_-_1988_Seoul-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<li><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Flag_of_Zambia_%281964%E2%80%931996%29.svg/22px-Flag_of_Zambia_%281964%E2%80%931996%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="22" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Flag_of_Zambia_%281964%E2%80%931996%29.svg/33px-Flag_of_Zambia_%281964%E2%80%931996%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Flag_of_Zambia_%281964%E2%80%931996%29.svg/44px-Flag_of_Zambia_%281964%E2%80%931996%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1400" />&#160;<a href="/wiki/Zambia_at_the_1988_Summer_Olympics" title="Zambia at the 1988 Summer Olympics">Zambia</a>&#160;<span style="font-size:90%;">(31)</span></li>
<li><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/22px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png" decoding="async" width="22" height="11" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/33px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/44px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1260" data-file-height="630" />&#160;<a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_at_the_1988_Summer_Olympics" title="Zimbabwe at the 1988 Summer Olympics">Zimbabwe</a>&#160;<span style="font-size:90%;">(31)</span></li></ul>
</div>
<p><span id="cnote_Note"><b><a href="#ref_Note">^</a></b></span>&#160;<b>Note:</b>&#160;Brunei participated in the Opening Ceremonies and Closing Ceremonies, marking its first appearance at the Olympic Games, but its delegation consisted of only one swimming official.<br />
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</center>
<ul><li>When the team from the Dominican Republic marched in during the Parade of Nations, the superimposed map erroneously showed the location of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medal_count">Medal count</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Medal count">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The official mascot for the 1988 Summer Olympic Games was <a href="/wiki/Hodori" title="Hodori">Hodori</a>. It was a stylized tiger designed by Kim Hyun as an amicable <a href="/wiki/Siberian_tiger" title="Siberian tiger">Amur tiger</a>, portraying the friendly and hospitable traditions of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Korean people">Korean people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodori_-_mascot_of_the_1988_Olympic_Summer_Games_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodori_-_mascot_of_the_1988_Olympic_Summer_Games-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Hodori's female version was called Hosuni.<sup id="cite_ref-Seoul_1988_-_Hodori_and_Hosuni_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seoul_1988_-_Hodori_and_Hosuni-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The name <span lang="ko" title="Korean language text">호돌이</span> <i>Hodori</i> was chosen from 2,295 suggestions sent in by the public. It is a <a href="/wiki/Compound_(linguistics)" title="Compound (linguistics)">compound</a> of <span lang="ko" title="Korean language text">호</span> <i>ho</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Korean_vocabulary" title="Sino-Korean vocabulary">Sino-Korean</a> <a href="/wiki/Bound_morpheme" class="mw-redirect" title="Bound morpheme">bound morpheme</a> for "tiger" (appearing also in the usual word <span lang="ko" title="Korean language text">호랑이</span> <i>horangi</i> for "tiger"), and <span lang="ko" title="Korean language text">돌이</span> <i>dori</i>, a diminutive for "boys".<sup id="cite_ref-Hodori_-_mascot_of_the_1988_Olympic_Summer_Games_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodori_-_mascot_of_the_1988_Olympic_Summer_Games-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast_rights">Broadcast rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Broadcast rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 1988 Games were covered by the following broadcasters:
</p>
